
============== high level task decomposition ================
[{'objective': 'Analyze the geometric properties of the convex equilateral hexagon with parallel opposite sides to establish relationships among its sides and angles.'}, {'objective': "Model the triangle formed by the extensions of sides AB, CD, and EF, expressing its side lengths in terms of the hexagon's side length."}, {'objective': "Use the given triangle side lengths (200, 240, 300) to set up equations relating these lengths to the hexagon's side length."}, {'objective': 'Solve the system of equations to determine the side length of the hexagon.'}]
============== task analysis ================
1. Extract and Summarize Given Information:
- The figure is a convex equilateral hexagon named ABCDEF.
- All pairs of opposite sides are parallel. Since the hexagon is equilateral, all its sides have the same length (unknown).
- The triangle mentioned is formed by the extensions of the sides AB, CD, and EF.
- The side lengths of this triangle are given as 200, 240, and 300.

2. Analyze Relationships Between Components:
- The hexagon is equilateral, so |AB| = |BC| = |CD| = |DE| = |EF| = |FA| = s (unknown side length).
- Opposite sides are parallel: AB || DE, BC || EF, CD || FA.
- The triangle formed by the extensions of AB, CD, and EF suggests these three lines intersect pairwise outside the hexagon, creating a triangle.
- The side lengths 200, 240, and 300 correspond to the distances between these intersection points.
- The parallelism and equilateral conditions impose strong geometric constraints, likely relating the hexagon's side length to the triangle's side lengths.

3. Identify the Field of Study:
- The problem lies primarily in Euclidean geometry.
- Subfields include polygon geometry, properties of convex polygons, and line geometry (intersections and extensions).
- The problem may also involve vector geometry or coordinate geometry for analysis.
- Such problems are common in mathematical competitions and advanced geometry studies.

4. Highlight Aspects Needing Clarification:
- The exact construction of the triangle from the extensions of AB, CD, and EF could be ambiguous without a diagram.
- It is not explicitly stated how the extensions intersect (e.g., which pairs of lines intersect to form the triangle's vertices).
- The problem assumes convexity and equilateral properties but does not specify angles or other measures.
- Potential challenges include handling the parallelism constraints and relating the hexagon's side length to the triangle's side lengths without additional data.

Let us define the side vectors as follows: AB = v1, BC = v2, CD = v3, DE = v4, EF = v5, FA = v6. Since the hexagon is closed, the sum of these vectors is zero: v1 + v2 + v3 + v4 + v5 + v6 = 0. The parallelism conditions imply: v1 is parallel to v4, so v4 = -v1 (since the hexagon is convex and the sides are oriented around the polygon, opposite sides point in opposite directions). Similarly, v2 is parallel to v5, so v5 = -v2, and v3 is parallel to v6, so v6 = -v3. Because all sides have length s, |v1| = |v2| = |v3| = s, and |v4| = |v5| = |v6| = s. Using the closure condition: v1 + v2 + v3 + v4 + v5 + v6 = v1 + v2 + v3 - v1 - v2 - v3 = 0, which is satisfied. Therefore, the hexagon can be represented by choosing three vectors v1, v2, v3 of length s, with directions such that the polygon is convex and the angles between them satisfy the convexity and parallelism constraints. The vertices can be expressed as: A = (0,0), B = A + v1, C = B + v2, D = C + v3, E = D - v1, F = E - v2. This representation ensures the hexagon is equilateral, convex, and has opposite sides parallel. The vectors v1, v2, v3 can be parameterized by their directions (angles) and the common length s. This formal vector representation captures all the given conditions and is consistent with the convexity and properties of the hexagon.\n\n### thinking by Chain-of-Thought Agent We1g:\nTo derive a formal vector or coordinate representation of the convex equilateral hexagon ABCDEF with opposite sides parallel, we start by representing the vertices as vectors in the plane: A, B, C, D, E, F.     from collections import Counter
    print("Task Requirement: ", taskInfo)
    sub_tasks = []

Let the side length be s. Since the hexagon is equilateral, all sides have length s. The directions of the sides must satisfy the parallelism conditions: AB || DE, BC || EF, and CD || FA. This implies the directions of sides come in three pairs of parallel vectors. We can represent the directions of sides as vectors with angles θ1, θ2, θ3 such that the sides are: AB along θ1=0°, BC along θ2, CD along θ3, DE along θ1+180°, EF along θ2+180°, and FA along θ3+180°. The sum of the vectors around the hexagon must be zero (closed polygon), so s*(v1 + v2 + v3 + (-v1) + (-v2) + (-v3))=0, which is trivially true. Intersection of EF and AB:\nSet r_EF(v) = r_AB(t):\n(s cos α + s cos β - s v cos α, s sin α + s sin β - s v sin α) = (s t, 0)\n\nFrom y:\ns sin α + s sin β - s v sin α = 0\n=> sin α + sin β - v sin α = 0\n=> v = (sin α + sin β) / sin α\n\nFrom x:\ns cos α + s cos β - s v cos α = s t\n=> t = cos α + cos β - v cos α\n\nSubstitute v:\nt = cos α + cos β - ((sin α + sin β)/sin α) * cos α\n\nThe intersection point R = (s t, 0) = (s [cos α + cos β - (sin α + sin β) cos α / sin α], 0)\n\nThese are the three vertices of the triangle formed by the extended lines AB, CD, and EF, expressed explicitly in terms of s, α, and β without approximations.\n\n### thinking by Chain-of-Thought Agent wS0w:\nWe have the parametric equations of the three lines AB, CD, and EF in terms of s, α, and β:\n\nLine AB: r_AB(t) = (s t, 0)\nLine CD: r_CD(u) = (s + s cos α + s u cos β, s sin α + s u sin β)\nLine EF: r_EF(v) = (s cos α + s cos β - s v cos α, s sin α + s sin β - s v sin α)\n\nWe want to find the intersection points of the pairs (AB, CD), (CD, EF), and (EF, AB).\n\n1.
